[3/18/25, 4:20:55 pm] Boss Imu: Support coordinators and NDIS coordinators encounter a wide range of questions in their daily roles, addressing practical, emotional, and administrative needs of participants. Below is a categorized list of common real-life scenarios and questions they might encounter:

### **1. Understanding the NDIS Plan**
- "How do I interpret my budget categories and what they cover?"  
- "Can I use my funding for [specific item/service], and how do I request it?"  
- "What’s the difference between Core, Capacity Building, and Capital Support budgets?"

### **2. Service Providers & Agreements**
- "How do I change service providers if I’m unsatisfied?"  
- "What should I include in a service agreement?"  
- "My support worker is unreliable. What are my options?"

### **3. Daily Living & Personal Care**
- "How do I find a support worker for personal care or household tasks?"  
- "Can I get funding for meal preparation or cleaning services?"  

### **4. Housing & Home Modifications**
- "Does my plan cover home modifications like ramps or bathroom rails?"  
- "What are my options for supported independent living (SIL)?"  

### **5. Transport & Mobility**
- "How do I apply for transport funding or a modified vehicle?"  
- "Can the NDIS fund travel costs to medical appointments?"  

### **6. Health & Therapy Services**
- "Will the NDIS cover physiotherapy or psychology sessions?"  
- "How do I coordinate NDIS supports with my Medicare-funded healthcare?"  

### **7. Employment & Education**
- "What supports are available to help me find a job?"  
- "Can the NDIS fund a classroom aide or tutoring for my child?"  

### **8. Social & Community Participation**
- "Are there social groups or recreational activities I can join using my funding?"  
- "How can I access cultural or community events relevant to my background?"  

### **9. Assistive Technology & Equipment**
- "How do I get approval for a communication device or wheelchair repair?"  
- "What’s the process for replacing broken equipment?"  

### **10. Plan Reviews & Changes**
- "My needs have changed—how do I request a plan review?"  
- "What evidence do I need to increase my funding for [specific support]?"  

### **11. Crisis & Emergency Support**
- "What do I do if my primary carer suddenly can’t support me?"  
- "Where can I get help during a housing or mental health crisis?"  

### **12. Budget Management**
- "How do I track my spending to avoid overspending?"  
- "What happens if I underspend in a budget category?"  

### **13. Rights, Advocacy & Complaints**
- "How do I lodge a complaint about a provider or NDIS decision?"  
- "Where can I find an advocate to help me navigate disputes?"  

### **14. Cultural & Language Needs**
- "Can I request a support worker who speaks my language?"  
- "Are there culturally specific services for my community?"  

### **15. Transition Planning**
- "What supports exist for moving from school to work?"  
- "How do I prepare for independent living as I age out of parental care?"  

### **16. Family & Carer Support**
- "Can my family member be paid as my support worker?"  
- "What resources are available for aging parents caring for an adult child?"  

### **17. Legal & Systemic Coordination**
- "How does the NDIS interact with Centrelink or aged care services?"  
- "What legal protections do I have against discrimination?"  

### **18. Technology & Portal Use**
- "How do I use the myplace portal to check my budget?"  
- "What should I do if I can’t access my plan online?"  

### **19. Assistance Animals**
- "Does the NDIS cover training or care for an assistance animal?"  
- "How do I get a guide dog approved in my plan?"  

### **20. Future Planning**
- "How can I ensure my supports adapt as my needs change over time?"  
- "What happens to my plan if I move to a different state?"  

These questions reflect the diverse responsibilities of support coordinators, who assist participants in navigating complex systems, advocating for their needs, and ensuring they maximize their NDIS plans to live independently and achieve their goals.

[3/24/25, 10:14:13 am] SkamberMuser: Here’s a concise summary of my research on existing NDIS apps, market insights, and a proposed plan for developing and marketing a new website, with all links embedded directly for easy access.
Existing NDIS Apps and Systems
	•	Official Tools:
	◦	my NDIS App (https://play.google.com/store/apps/details?id=au.gov.ndis, https://apps.apple.com/au/app/my-ndis/id1518926938): Free app for participants to manage plans and claims, designed with accessibility in mind (https://www.ndis.gov.au/participants/using-your-plan/managing-your-plan/my-ndis-mobile-app/making-ndis-app-participants), but users note usability challenges (https://apps.apple.com/au/app/my-ndis/id1518926938).
	◦	NDIS Portals (https://improvements.ndis.gov.au/participants/my-ndis-participant-portal-and-app, https://www.ndis.gov.au/providers/working-with-ndis-providers/provider-portal): For plan and claim management, though often criticized for being unintuitive.
	•	Third-Party Tools:
	◦	ShiftCare (https://shiftcare.com/solutions/ndis-providers-software): Provider-focused with rostering and billing, starting at AUD 9/user/month.
	◦	MyCareSpace (https://mycarespace.com.au/): Links participants with providers, offering a directory and resources (https://mycarespace.com.au/business-directory).
	◦	Others like SupportAbility (https://www.supportability.com.au/) and CareMaster (https://www.caremaster.com.au/) serve providers with advanced features but higher costs.
Market Research Insights
	•	Market Size: Over 500,000 participants, growing yearly (https://dataresearch.ndis.gov.au/reports-and-analyses/market-monitoring), within a multi-billion-dollar market.
	•	User Needs: Participants seek simple, accessible tools; providers want efficiency. Gaps include usability and lack of AI features (https://dataresearch.ndis.gov.au/research-and-evaluation/market-stewardship-and-employment/markets-and-innovations-research).
	•	Opportunity: A user-friendly, accessible platform could fill these gaps, especially for participants.
Website and Marketing Plan
	•	Website Idea: A participant-focused platform with plan management, an AI-enhanced provider directory, and top-tier accessibility (e.g., voice commands). Freemium model—free basics, premium at AUD 10/month.
	•	Marketing: Leverage social media (Facebook, X), SEO, and partnerships with disability groups (https://nds.org.au/). Launch with a beta test and referral program.
	•	USP: “The most accessible NDIS management tool, built for you.”
Next Steps
	•	Validate with user feedback, create a landing page, and develop a prototype. Full details are in the attached research.
Let me know your feedback or if you want adjustments!
Cheers, [Your Name]

Problem

Getting construction approval in Sydney (and possibly greater Australia) is time-consuming, varying by council, and involves filling multiple redundant forms manually.

The Solution

A web-based AI-powered assistant that:
 • Takes in basic project data and architectural briefs
 • Auto-detects the local council
 • Identifies the required forms and permits
 • Pre-fills forms using AI
 • Generates downloadable .docx or .zip files


MVP Features
 • Frontend (multi-step form wizard)
 • Backend to manage council requirements and documents processing
 • Council detection via suburb mapping
 • AI prompt generation using OpenAI
 • Smart brief/document extraction
 • Council rules stored in editable JSON
 • Dynamic form-filling logic
 • Export filled forms as ZIP files
 • Simple admin route to manage council logic
 • Password-protected admin panel
 • Auto-versioning of filled files and rule changes


Possible Future Enhancements
 • CMS backend for structured rule and user management
 • Email delivery of forms
 • File previews (PDF or HTML)
 • Council portal submission APIs (long-term)
 • Form completion logs & analytics


Product Monetization Options

1. Pay-Per-Use
 • Charge per bundle generation
 • Simple Stripe checkout before download

2. Free Trial + Subscription
 • X free bundles per user
 • Then monthly plans

3. Partner Program
 • License or monthly API access fees


MVP Development Estimate

Todos - Checklists
Council-specific form requirements
Suburb-to-council mapping
Sample client briefs and form data for questionnaires
[4/24/25, 9:52:25 pm] Boss Imu: What is this?
[4/24/25, 9:55:49 pm] SkamberMuser: AI Form Filler MVP Workflow Overview

This automated workflow extracts important data from uploaded construction-related PDF documents (like BASIX and Drawings), sends it to Airtable for review, and preps it for final form generation.


How It Works (Step-by-Step)
	1.	Webhook Trigger (Start Point)
The process starts when a new PDF is uploaded (BASIX + Drawing), and a webhook is triggered—usually from an internal tool or app.
	2.	Extract Text with AWS Textract
The PDFs are stored in cloud storage (e.g., S3 or alternatives). AWS Textract reads the text from these files.
	3.	Extract Key Information
AI logic extracts important fields from each document, such as:
	•	Project Name
	•	Lot Number
	•	Water Score
	•	Site Area
	4.	Merge Extracted Data
The information from both documents (BASIX + Drawings) is merged into a single structured dataset.
	5.	Save to Airtable (Review Stage)
This merged data is then saved to Airtable:
	•	Airtable acts as a central dashboard for the team to review and correct any data.
	•	Fields like status are set to “Pending Review” to track the workflow stage.
	6.	(Next Steps - Future)
After team review, another automation will fill out final forms (e.g., PDFs, government forms) using the cleaned data and move the project to completion

[7/7/25, 8:37:41 am] Boss Imu: Prompt for AI
[7/7/25, 8:37:42 am] Boss Imu: You are a marketing AI tasked with creating a printed leaflet for a new diabetes medication in Bangladesh. Write content in a formal, factual tone suitable for doctors, and include a Bengali translation for patient information sections.

- **Product Name:** Empatab M 5/500 – (Empagliflozin 5 mg + Metformin HCl 500 mg) tablet  
- **Therapeutic Area:** Type 2 Diabetes Mellitus  
- **Key Benefits:** 
  1. Excellent glycemic control (significantly lowers HbA1c)  
  2. Provides cardiovascular benefits (reduces risk of heart failure and CV death)  
  3. Improved patient compliance (once-daily dosing)  
- **Clinical Data to Include:** ADA guideline: *“Aim for HbA1c <7%”* [oai_citation:16‡diabetes.org](https://diabetes.org/about-diabetes/a1c#:~:text=When%20it%20comes%20to%20the,that%20is%20less%20than%207); EMPA-REG outcome: *“38% reduction in CV death with empagliflozin”* [oai_citation:17‡cardiab.biomedcentral.com](https://cardiab.biomedcentral.com/articles/10.1186/s12933-022-01575-9#:~:text=Cardioprotective%20benefits%20of%20GLDs%20were,file%20%2048%3A%20Table%20S1); 63% of patients reached target A1c in 24 weeks (study X).  
- **Regulatory Note:** “DGDA approved. For healthcare professional use only.”  
- **Format:** 
  - Title and slogan (English & Bengali)  
  - Brief intro paragraph  
  - Bullet points for benefits (in English)  
  - A short section “বিস্তারিত তথ্য” (Bengali for “Detailed Information”) summarizing in Bengali for patients.  
  - Footer with references and disclaimer.

[7/7/25, 8:37:42 am] Boss Imu: *Data Sources for Training the AI*

To train the AI effectively, a diverse range of textual and visual data is needed. Key source categories include local pharma literature, regulatory documents, clinical guidelines, marketing collateral, and image libraries:
	•	Local Pharma Company Literature: Brochures, product monographs, and marketing write-ups from top Bangladeshi companies (e.g. Incepta, Beximco, Square, Renata). These often contain drug descriptions, indications, doses, and promotional claims. For example, Square Pharmaceuticals publishes a comprehensive Product Guide with abridged prescribing info for all its products ￼, and Incepta’s website provides product details (indications, usage, etc.) for each medicine ￼. Such sources teach the AI the tone and content of local product communications.
	•	Regulatory and Compliance Documents: Bangladesh’s Directorate General of Drug Administration (DGDA) issues guidelines that marketing must comply with. The pivotal Code of Pharmaceutical Marketing Practices (CPMP), first adopted in 1994, sets ethical standards for promotion ￼. It aligns with international norms (IFPMA Code) and ensures companies promote drugs responsibly. Also relevant is the Drug Control Ordinance (1982) which prohibits any drug advertisement without prior government approval ￼. These regulations inform the AI about what claims or wording are acceptable. For instance, promotional materials in Bangladesh are physician-oriented and cannot be advertised to the general public without authorization (e.g. DGDA requires a statement of approval on brochures). Indeed, local promotional brochures carry disclaimers like “circulated with prior approval of the licensing authority” and include reference citations and prescribing information in fine print, reflecting these rules (as seen in an Incepta brochure example).
	•	Clinical Guidelines and Medical Data: To make scientifically accurate claims, the AI should learn from clinical practice guidelines (especially those often cited in local marketing) and key trial data. Examples: the American Diabetes Association (ADA) standards for diabetes, which recommend a target HbA1c < 7% for most adults ￼, or cardiovascular risk guidelines from ACC/AHA. Bangladesh marketing often cites such global guidelines to legitimize claims. It’s common to reference landmark clinical trials that demonstrate a drug’s benefits – for example, SGLT2 inhibitor trials showing reduced cardiovascular mortality. Training data can include summaries of trials like EMPA-REG (where empagliflozin showed a 38% reduction in CV death ￼) or local clinical consensus documents. Incorporating these ensures the AI can generate content like “According to ADA 2023 guidelines, achieving HbA1c below 7% is recommended to reduce complications” or “Empagliflozin has shown a 38% reduction in cardiovascular death in trials ￼.”
[7/7/25, 8:37:43 am] Boss Imu: Design and Layout AI Tools: For generating visual layouts and graphics, one could leverage generative models and design AI platforms:
	•	Image Generation Models: Tools like DALL·E 3 or Stable Diffusion can create illustrations of medications, logos, or patient scenarios. For instance, a diffusion model fine-tuned on existing pharma advertisement images might generate plausible brochure backgrounds or mock patient-doctor scenes. These can be used to suggest visuals that the AI agent can include or recommend (with the final selection likely reviewed by a human designer for quality). Logo generation can also be attempted with generative models by training on a dataset of pharma logos.
	•	Layout Generators: While in early stages, there are AI research projects on graphic layout generation. In practice, using template-based generation with AI assistance might be more feasible. For example, the AI could output structured data (like JSON or HTML/CSS code) representing a brochure’s layout – sections for images, headings, body text, footnotes – which can then be rendered with design software. Tools such as Adobe InDesign or Canva have started offering AI features (e.g. suggesting color palettes or auto-generating a layout given text) that could be integrated. The agent could interface with these: e.g. produce copy text and suggest “insert product image here, use company logo at top-right, apply blue theme matching diabetes branding.” While not a model per se, frameworks like LangChain could be used to chain the LLM (for content) with an image generator (for visuals) and a rule-based formatter to output a cohesive designed piece.
	•	Multi-modal Models: Emerging multi-modal systems (like GPT-4’s vision capabilities or Google’s PaLM-V2 Unicorn which handles text and image) could be explored. These models can interpret images and generate text or vice versa. For example, a multi-modal model could take a rough template image of a brochure and fill in text, or generate an image given a text prompt about a packaging design.
	•	Domain-Specific Resources: There are also specialized tools worth noting:
	•	Medication Databases (for accuracy): Incorporating an NLP model that was fine-tuned on drug databases (like FDA labels or the Bangladesh National Formulary) ensures that when the AI writes scientific/regulatory content, it lists indications, side effects, etc., correctly. Models like Med7 (NER model) could help the AI recognize drug names and medical terms in context.
	•	Translation APIs or Models: Since bilingual output is needed, one could use models like MarianMT or Google’s translation model fine-tuned for English↔️Bengali medical text to post-process or assist the main LLM’s output. This ensures the Bengali translations of technical terms are accurate (e.g. “diabetes” -> “ডায়াবেটিস”, “blood sugar” -> “রক্তের চিনির মাত্রা”, etc.).
	•	Text-to-Speech or Video Tools (optional): If the marketing materials extend to digital media (e.g. narrated videos or interactive content), tools like Synthesia (for AI video with avatars speaking Bengali/English) or text-to-speech engines with Bengali support might be useful. (This is beyond print collateral, but could be a future extension.)

[7/7/25, 10:37:29 am] SkamberMuser: A Sample Workflow with PharmaBrand AI
Imagine you are the marketer. Here’s how you would use the bot:
You Open the PharmaBrand AI Console and Start a New Project.
You type: "Launch new product. Molecule: Empagliflozin 10mg + Linagliptin 5mg. Therapeutic Area: Type 2 Diabetes."
The Strategic Insights Engine Activates.
The Bot Responds: "Analyzing the T2DM combination market in Bangladesh. Key competitors are [Competitor A, Competitor B]. Successful brands in this space emphasize cardiovascular safety and once-daily convenience. The color blue is heavily associated with diabetes; we could use a unique color like teal or orange to differentiate. The EMPA-REG and CARMELINA trials are the most frequently cited data points for these molecules."
The Bot Generates a Full Brand Package Proposal.
Brand Name Suggestions: Empalina, Glyxambi-D, Emplia-Go.
Logo Concepts: Presents 3 logo options in a teal and white color scheme.
Slogan: "Dual Action for Complete Glycemic and Cardio-Renal Control. / দ্বৈত কার্যকারিতায় ডায়াবেটিস ও হৃদপিণ্ডের সুরক্ষায়।"
Draft Literature: A full, two-page leaflet is generated, citing the relevant clinical trials, with all sections (Intro, Benefits, Bengali patient info, References, DGDA disclaimer) pre-filled.
Layout Mockup: A visual template of the leaflet is displayed.
You Review and Refine.
You type: "I like the name 'Empalina'. For the logo, use concept #2 but make the teal slightly darker. In the literature, add a bullet point about renal benefits."
The Bot Instantly Updates All Assets.
Within seconds, you have a revised, complete branding kit ready for final human review and submission to the regulatory authority.

THE ORIGIN OF JUPURR 😺💨
"I didn’t launch. I slipped out."


Once upon a liquidity fart, Weremeow microwaved a burrito inside the Jupiter core engine room. The radiation mixed with leftover cat hair, some unvested JUP tokens, and exactly one very suspicious can of expired Fancy Feast.
BOOM.

A furball the size of Texas launched itself out of the wormhole and crash-landed in the middle of the Jupiter Studio dashboard.

The devs screamed.
The server meowed.
And $JUPURR was born.

🧪 JUPURR’S BIO
“Name’s Jupurr. I’m part cat, part gas giant, all problem.”

[9/4/25, 10:29:00 am] SkamberMuser: Here’s a breakdown of content types AI social media influencers should prioritize in 2025, grounded in the latest analytics and trends:

⸻

Key Content Trends for 2025

1. Video Remains King—But Long-Form Is Making a Comeback
	•	Short-form (TikTok, Reels, Shorts) continues to dominate for rapid engagement.  ￼
	•	However, there’s a growing appetite for long-form content, like vlogs, podcasts, and livestreams, which allow deeper storytelling and audience retention.  ￼ ￼ ￼

** Recommendation**: Build a hybrid strategy—maintain attention-grabbing short videos, supplemented by occasional long-form pieces that show personality and depth.

⸻

2. Generative AI Is Fully Integrated
	•	Generative AI tools are now central to content creation, providing speed and scalability. 69% of marketers see AI as revolutionary.  ￼
	•	AI isn’t just behind the scenes—it’s often visible in visuals and writing (e.g., 71% of images and 54% of long-form posts are AI-generated).  ￼

** Recommendation**: Use AI to rapidly generate ideas, drafts, visuals, and caption variations. Combine AI tools with human insight to ensure creativity and authenticity shine through.

⸻

3. Authenticity & Nostalgia Drive Engagement
	•	Audiences crave sincerity over showy performance. The return of “millennial cringe” shows value in vulnerability when done sincerely.  ￼
	•	Nostalgia—especially early-2000s vibes—is surging, reflecting a broader cultural longing for real connection.  ￼

** Recommendation**: Embrace imperfect, emotional storytelling. Use nostalgic hooks and self-aware humor to build genuine connection.

⸻

4. AI Influencers—A Double-Edged Sword
	•	Brands are increasingly turning to hyper-realistic AI influencers, drawn by cost and scale.  ￼
	•	Yet there’s mounting backlash over perceived inauthenticity and damage to trust.  ￼

** Recommendation**: If you’re using AI persona elements, be transparent—clearly distinguish human-led vs. AI-driven content. Authenticity remains your best asset.

⸻

5. Niche Trends & Community-Driven Moments
	•	Movements like “RushTok” (sorority recruitment TikTok content) show how niche micro-communities can spark massive branded content cycles.  ￼
	•	Leveraging trendy slang, memes, or subculture cues can amplify emotional engagement—but tread lightly to stay authentic.  ￼

** Recommendation**: Monitor grassroots micro-trends, contribute with tailored, respectful content, and avoid jumping on every bandwagon.

⸻

6. Social Listening Unlocks Micro-Viral Strategy
	•	Listening tools help identify the next big thing before it pops—or when it’s already peaking.  ￼
	•	Micro-virality—subtle, targeted trend involvement—is now preferred over broad, fleeting virality.  ￼

** Recommendation**: Use real-time feedback to guide your creative content—capitalize on trends with precision, not blanket mimicry.

⸻

Content Strategy Summary

Focus Area	Content Approach
Video Mix	Short (for discovery) + Long (for storytelling and depth)
AI Integration	Use AI for efficiency, but finalize content with human quality and nuance
Authenticity & Nostalgia	Share vulnerable moments or nostalgic callbacks in your own unique tone
Ethical AI Influencer Use	If using AI personas, label them clearly to maintain trust
Trend Responsiveness	Spot niche trends early and participate thoughtfully
Data-Driven Iteration	Let social listening guide you toward content that resonates


⸻

Final Takeaway

For AI social media influencers in 2025, the winning content is a thoughtful blend:
	•	Be efficient and creative with AI—but keep your human edge.
	•	Move viewers quickly with short clips, but retain them with richer, long-form storytelling.
	•	Build trust through transparency, vulnerability, and nostalgia.
	•	Engage trends with data-driven precision—not for clout, but for connection.

Let me know the influencer’s style, niche, or goals—I’d be happy to help craft prompts, content pillars, or even sample scripts to fit!

	•	Expenses:

	•	$5 for medical expenses (ankle dislocation)
	•	Credits Usage (12,000 total allocation):
	•	Images at 30 credits per generation
	•	Veo3 videos at 1,500 credits per generation

I used most of the credits yesterday while generating videos. Some content restrictions caused violations, which required switching to other models (Kling, Wan). However, Veo3 remains the most effective option, offering both high-quality video and integrated voice output. Other models lack these features unless paired with third-party tools like 11Labs, which would add costs.

I now have a clearer understanding of how credits are consumed and why they depleted so quickly. I purchased some additional credits, but they only covered a limited number of extra generations.

Recommendation:
To reduce costs and improve sustainability, I suggest exploring platforms like Fal.ai or Higgsfield, which provide access to multiple models for both images and videos at significantly lower rates (around $0.03 per generation). This would make ongoing production more cost-effective.

[3/9/26, 1:21:12 am] SkamberMuser: These 5 mistakes cost homeowners THOUSANDS. Don't be one of them.

❌ MISTAKE 1: Cramped kitchen with no workspace
✅ FIX: Design the kitchen triangle (stove-sink-fridge) with minimum 1.2m clearance

❌ MISTAKE 2: Poor flow between living spaces
✅ FIX: Create clear circulation paths, avoid bottlenecks

❌ MISTAKE 3: Wasted space in awkward corners
✅ FIX: Built-in storage solutions, custom joinery

❌ MISTAKE 4: No natural light in key rooms
✅ FIX: Strategic window placement, consider light wells

❌ MISTAKE 5: Ignoring the site orientation
✅ FIX: Design for your specific block — sun, breeze, views

The difference between a good floor plan and a great one? It's not luck. It's experience.

Posting Days: Monday, Wednesday, Friday
Goal: Educate homeowners, showcase expertise, and attract project inquiries

Monday — Educational / Tips

Type: Carousel

Week 1 Example:
Post: 5 Design Mistakes That Cost Homeowners Thousands
Slides:
	1.	Hook: “5 Design Mistakes That Cost Homeowners Thousands”
	2.	Mistake #1 – Cramped kitchen
	3.	Mistake #2 – Poor room flow
	4.	Mistake #3 – Wasted corners
	5.	Mistake #4 – No natural light
	6.	Mistake #5 – Ignoring site orientation
	7.	CTA

Goal: Post saves & shares

Wednesday — Process / Value

Type: Carousel / Infographic

Week 1 Example:
Post: How Residential Drafting Works (4-Step Process)
Slides:
	1.	Cover: “How Residential Drafting Works”
	2.	Step 1 – Initial Consultation
	3.	Step 2 – Concept Design
	4.	Step 3 – Drafting & Documentation
	5.	Step 4 – Council Approval
	6.	CTA

Goal: Establish authority & trust

Friday — Project / Visual Showcase

Type: Image or Carousel

Week 1 Example:
Post: Modern Home Extension
Content: Showcase extension render
Caption:
“From concept to reality. This extension maximizes natural light, space, and indoor-outdoor living.”

Goal: Inspire and attract inquiries

Additional Weeks

Week 2:
	•	Monday: 3 Ways to Bring More Natural Light Into Your Home
	•	Wednesday: What a Draftsman Actually Does
	•	Friday: Before vs After Extension

Week 3:
	•	Monday: Small Block Design Tips
	•	Wednesday: Why Floor Plans Matter
	•	Friday: 3D Visualization Example

Feed Layout Strategy

Tip	Process	Project
Tip	Authority	Render
Tip	Process	Project

Result: Balanced, professional, and visually consistent feed

Posting Times (NSW, Australia)
	•	7 PM – 9 PM AEST
	•	12 PM – 1 PM AEST

Content Goals
	•	Educational posts: Generate saves and shares
	•	Process/Value posts: Build credibility and trust
	•	Project/Visual posts: Inspire homeowners and attract clients

Monthly Output: 12 posts

When planning isn't quite right, it can lead to:
Unexpected design changes that cost a fortune
Frustrating delays in getting approvals
Confusion and missteps once building actually starts
That's precisely why having really clear, professional drafting plans is so crucial. It's the foundation you need before any physical work begins.
At ZenDrafting, we get it. We love helping homeowners and builders take their initial ideas and transform them into precise, council-ready plans. Our goal is to make the whole process smoother for everyone involved.
With solid planning from the start, you'll find yourself:
✔   Cutting down on expensive errors
✔   Making your design process much more efficient
✔   Stepping onto the build site with genuine confidence
Whether you're dreaming of a new home, tackling a big renovation, or adding an extension, getting the plans right upfront truly makes all the difference.

[5/7/26, 7:33:04 am] Boss Imu: 🏡 Restoring, Not Just Demolishing — Our Approach in Moree

We are currently working on 3 fire-damaged residential projects in Moree, focusing on smart and sustainable redevelopment rather than complete demolition.

Instead of removing the entire structure, our approach is to carefully assess and retain the parts of the building that remain structurally sound and suitable for the proposed new development.

✅ Structural elements that can be safely restored are being preserved
✅ Damaged sections are being demolished and redesigned
✅ New works are planned to comply with current Australian Standards and council requirements
✅ Reducing unnecessary demolition helps minimise waste and project costs
✅ Preserving existing structures can also maintain character while supporting modern living outcomes

Through careful planning, structural assessment, and compliant design solutions, these projects demonstrate how damaged properties can be transformed into safe, functional, and high-quality developments.

This approach not only supports sustainable construction practices but also creates better long-term value for property owners and investors.

📩 If you have a damaged property, renovation project, or redevelopment opportunity in Moree, feel free to contact us to discuss design, drafting, DA approvals, and development solutions.
